  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b5bbf950-0da1-4d88-a8f6-f8cf24e83af0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText8894643349899578244" style="display:none">The Foxes are a fractured mess, but their latest disaster might be the miracle they've always needed to come together as a team. The one person standing in their way is Andrew, and the only one who can break through his personal barriers is Neil.<br /><br />Except Andrew doesn't give up anything for free and Neil is terrible at trusting anyone but himself. The two don't have much time to come to terms with their situation before outside forces start tearing them apart. Riko is intent on destroying Neil's fragile new life, and the Foxes have just become collateral damage.<br /><br />Neil's days are numbered, but he's learning the hard way to go down fighting for what he believes in, and Neil believes in Andrew even if Andrew won't believe in himself.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2302802455" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2302802455?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18743272-the-raven-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2302802455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1867141339959683000"><b>read 3 [jan 2020]</b><br/>this reread was basically dedicated to me panic-laughing out loud at all the incredibly golden snark moments of Josten stupidity while wearing headphones and listening to the audiobooks while quietly dying inside so I match Neil 👌🏻<br/><br/><br/><b>read 2 [feb 2019]</b><br/>the fact that I am no longer breathing just confirms how this series is absolutely my everything and I am trash for it and basically a wreck of emotions. I swear I love these dysfunctional damaged traumatised kids so much <i>it hurts me</i>. </span>
  <span id="freeText1867141339959683000" style="display:none"><b>read 3 [jan 2020]</b><br />this reread was basically dedicated to me panic-laughing out loud at all the incredibly golden snark moments of Josten stupidity while wearing headphones and listening to the audiobooks while quietly dying inside so I match Neil 👌🏻<br /><br /><br /><b>read 2 [feb 2019]</b><br />the fact that I am no longer breathing just confirms how this series is absolutely my everything and I am trash for it and basically a wreck of emotions. I swear I love these dysfunctional damaged traumatised kids so much <i>it hurts me</i>. And rereading just made me see all these subplots and extra hints and foreshadowing that I didn't the first time. It's so so excellent. And I just CRY for Neil. Like he views everyone as so messed up...but this kid. <i>This kid</i>. He is a wreck. And his terrified looks when people are kind to him and how he gets totally like "????" when he realises the Foxes refer to him as their <i>friend</i>. <br /><br />im crying ok yes yes<br /><br />(Also Coach HOLDING HIM THROUGH HIS PANIC ATTACK AT THE END.)<br /><br />I'm going to just curl into a ball of emotions for 10 seconds and then get to my absolutely favourite book of the series... (But also?? I do not want this to end ajfkdslad. Can I just reread forever.)<br /><br /><br /><br />*:·ﾟ✧*:·ﾟ✧<br /><br /><b>Read 1 || Feb 2018</b><br /><br /><br /><b>HOLY WOW THAT GOT BRUTALLY DARK AT THE END THERE I'M REELING.</b> Honestly I don't even know why I'm loving these books so much ah haha. I actually loathe sports. And the writing could be <i>so</i> much better...but the characters have 500% won me and life is too short not to admit I love Neil Frikkin' Liar Josten and I just????? I need to know what happens. I can't stop thinking about them.<br /><br />ALSO IT GOT REALLY BLOODILY DARK and I do like books with a sidedish of cookies from the dark side and also my feels splattered all over the ground.<br /><br /><b>LIST OF NOTABLE THINGS:</b><br />• Coach Wymack broke and called them "my kids" ah haha HAHAH I knew that was going to happen<br />• this hit a lot of dark topics<br />• why don't we just see if we can make everyone cry that's nice<br />• Kevin's panic attacks are so real<br />• Neil's just getting more defiant and fiesty each book, because people CARE about him and he's starting to believe it<br />• Neil's panic attack over the phone and then Andrew/Nicky working him through it wast just afjdkslad<br />• afjsdkaldj<br />• (I'm a good reviewer hush)<br />• everyone's birth-families suck wow<br />• Nicky existing, what a gift<br />• Aaron actually getting a story line this time instead of being an uninteresting stump<br />• THE TIME NEIL DRESSED UP AS A ZOMBIE COWBOY BECAUSE NICKY SAID TO FOR HALLOWEEN<br />• f a m i l y<br />• the family you choose &lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3<br /><br /><br /><b>I'm still NOT DOWN with the ableist language.</b><br />There's no need, ever. Just... do not.<br /><br /><b>And again I do point to the writing and ask why it is being a lettuce.</b><br />There was just tons of unnecessary details?! Like we don't need to see Neil putting the key in the ignition ffs just move forward, mate. And there's a LOT of unnecessary pieces like that. It's tedious. Plus the writing would've absolutely exploded my fragile little soul if it'd honed in on developing the 5 senses and giving the characters more quirks and descriptions. Like when it <i>does</i> do the descriptions, it's good and punchy and right. But thEY'RE TOO RARE. Things like Neil grabbing his phone in his pocket to remind him he can call for help --&gt; punchy writing. <b>I wanted way way more of that.</b> And yet here I am...giving it 5 stars anyway. LMAO SEE WHAT THE CHARACTERS HAVE DONE TO ME.<br /><br /><b>No one is spared in this one, omg no one.</b><br />Again it's probably not YA even if Neil is 18 ah ahha just excuse me while I flap about unable to shelve it right. There's drugs, alcohol abuse, violence, rape, and some torture (but mostly off page). And it absolutely just splatters your feels okay. THINGS GO DOWN AND I AM NOT OK. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[WYMACK RESCUING NEIL AT THE END IS BREAKING ME INTO VERY SMOL AND VERY BROKEN PIECES AND NEIL IS NOT OKAY AND THEY CUT NEIL UP AND TATTOOED HIS FACE AND WHAT ARE WE GOING TO DO. I'M HAVING A MOMENT. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b> And it's even hard to say why I like the characters?!</b><br />They're all problematic little monsters and I don't condone any of their actions haha and mostly their friendships range from supportive to nearly abusive. But it's the complexity of actually writing about "broken" people and diving into the cause-and-effect of what's going on. They just feel so real and so well BUILT that I'm really invested in their lives. And Neil is a tragic darling who is so freaking obvious. <br /><br />aLSO I FOUND MY SHIP IT BETTER SAIL IN BOOK 3 OR <br /><br />(Also secretly glad there was less Exy in this because I still don't even care about the sport game. Why am I enjoying a series about JOCKS?! I have no idea.)<br /><br /><b>Basically this book is a mess and I am too wow.</b><br />I will just go admit I'm on the floor and go order buy book 3, goodbye for now.<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>"Kid, you're killing me," Nicky said. "Why do you always get that deer-in-the-headlights look when someone does something nice for you?</blockquote></span>

  <span id="freeText1170070511954404945" style="display:none"><i>“I am a bad person trying very hard to be a good person.”</i><br /><br />Oh wow I don't know what to say. So let's start with a big fat <b>trigger warning</b>: Rape, Violence, Abuse! I was not prepared.<br /><br /><i>The Raven King</i> was even better than <i>The Foxhole Court</i>. The plot picked up, but the romance didn't. Still no trace of it on the horizon.<br />However, it was intense, thrilling and 100% shocking. I couldn't stop reading, was up till late at night and went to sleep still thinking about it.<br />The Foxes are such interesting characters, it never gets boring. I'm totally rooting for them, but their issues are endless. I just hope they all get their happy ending. The Ravens however - well I hope they all die gruesome deaths. I hope Riko dies a thousand of them.<br /><br />I finished this and started the sequel right away. This series is going to destroy me.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_2281948055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2281948055" />
    <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments"><img alt="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554228831p2/67920559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2281948055?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments">Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=better-late-than-never">better-late-than-never</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=family-power">family-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=try-again-later">try-again-later</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=unlikeable-characters">unlikeable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=story-with-sports">story-with-sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=thin-line-between-love-and-hate">thin-line-between-love-and-hate</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281948055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer737652343084747550"><i>
  <b>“He was their family. They were his. They were worth every cut and bruise and scream.” </b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520271313i/25166321.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This review has been a long time coming, it feels like I've been <s>trying to</s> reading this book for the longest time, and then I fell sick for a while so I couldn't actually function properly. <i>The Raven King</i> was by far better than it's predecessor. I loved so many elements of it and although the overall components helped boost my love for the characters - I still felt like it ran short in some facets. <br/><br/>I buddy</span>
  <span id="freeText737652343084747550" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“He was their family. They were his. They were worth every cut and bruise and scream.” </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520271313i/25166321.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This review has been a long time coming, it feels like I've been <s>trying to</s> reading this book for the longest time, and then I fell sick for a while so I couldn't actually function properly. <i>The Raven King</i> was by far better than it's predecessor. I loved so many elements of it and although the overall components helped boost my love for the characters - I still felt like it ran short in some facets. <br><br>I buddy read this with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/41756564-clara" rel="nofollow noopener">my heart and my damn soul.</a> Clara, you're the best kind of person and thanks for putting up with my shit. Pretty sure everyone needs one of you in their life &lt;3 <br><br><u>Note</u>: All rights belong to the different artists that have created the (fucking amazing) fanart attached to this review.<br>__________<br><br><u>
  <b>Bleeding Orange </b>
</u><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520271313i/25166323.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"We're your teammates. We're here to help you with whatever you need, whether it's this or games or general stress. We've all got different experiences, but we're used to needing help. We're just not used to getting it. But you've got us now." </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>History has shown that putting a group of misfits together and seeing them evolve into a family always works out. All the 80's movies that I grew up with like Stand By Me, The Breakfast Club, The Outsiders, and even Ferris Bueller's Day Off... they all have that mischief and uncanny representation of 'not fitting in' that makes my heart soar. <br><br><b>The Foxes have that. </b><br><br>That's why this is probably my favourite element of this series, the fact that Neil Josten acts as the catalyst to bring together this hell-bent on winning team.<br>Although it was very unrealistic at many parts, the book deals with heavy and sensitive themes and I want to raise all the glasses to that. <br><br>One problem that I really had was the deal with Andrew and the drugs, as I can't really talk about this without spilling spoilers - I just thought not only was it unrealistic, but there are much better ways to handle that topic and I feel like the author could have done that better. I also think the way that they treated his health as something secondary to playing a match etc. was unacceptable. It almost felt like a hurdle and an issue rather than a part of him that he is dealing with. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Wymack didn't care if he had nine Foxes or twenty-five. He'd stand behind them until the bitter, bloody end."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><u>
  <b>The Writing</b>
</u><br>So, one of the points that both Clara and I noticed was the comparative improvement of writing between book 1 and this one. The writing didn't seem as amateur, and I loved how every chapter left me with some sort of tingly feeling. <br>The sport itself is getting a bit more clear in my head, I need to detach Exy from Lacrosse but that's just a personal problem. It was great seeing the writing style and prose of Sakavic shine through her third person narration. <br><br>The development between Neil and Andrew made this all endurable. I could see the little things and although the 'monsters' still have a lot of tension with Neil especially, I loved that group dynamic. If ever there was a time where slow burn frustrated the shit out of me - this would be it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520271313i/25166325._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Andrew is a bit of a conundrum for me. I loved that we got a little bit more about his past in this addition, simply because it allowed me to empathize with him a bit more. I have to admit, in book 1 - I had mixed feelings about both Andrew and Kevin - but in TRK I found myself liking Kevin more and having the same confusion about what I think of Andrew. <br><br><b>But here's what I think</b> - I think that was the point. I think the reader is supposed to feel a mixture of feelings with Andrew because that's just the type of character he is. He's the kind of guy you love to hate and hate to love. Especially with everything he went through, you're left with the question of how every action he does has a hidden meaning underneath. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520271313i/25166322._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Thanks, but I can handle him," Neil said.<br>"We noticed," Dan said dryly.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Thematic Paint</b>
</u><br>So I feel like there are enough reviews out there clearly stating that there are major trigger warnings when you read this series in general - it's not something that gets skirted around with. During the end, the plot picked up into some really dark themes. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Neil's grief was a knife spinning circles in his stomach, tearing him to shreds from the inside out until he could barely breathe.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520271313i/25166324.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just want to say that during the first 50% of this book, I was bored. Unpopular opinion (as usual) time but I really felt like DNFing - and maybe that was because I was really ill and just had no motivation to read. However, I also think that as soon as I passed a key plot marker, I got interested. It felt like relief because I really did not want to rate this book anything less than 3 stars. That felt like being too harsh and too cruel. <br><br>It went a lot like the last book, and although I don't know if I am picking up the third book right away - I am sure going to read it some time or the other! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Some of the strongest people I've known are women." </b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="737652343084747550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2461492292" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2461492292" />
    <a title="may ➹" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68157476-may"><img alt="may ➹" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538949856p2/68157476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2461492292?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ➹" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ➹" href="/user/show/68157476-may">may ➹</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<div id="review_2972016212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2972016212" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78730059-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545995679p2/78730059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2972016212?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/78730059-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=squad-goals">squad-goals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=diversity">diversity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=friends">friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78730059-lara?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2972016212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6703261688591718306"><a href='https://bookishreviewsblog.blogspot.com/2019/09/nora-sakavic-raven-king-foxhole-court.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>My review </a><br/><br/><i>"They were exhausted, sore, and more than a little disappointed by their loss, but the Foxes left the stadium feeling like champions.”</i><br/><br/><br/>They are every fucking inch the champions. Excuse me, where can I sign the adoption papers for the entire Palmetto State University Team? I am a complete fucking mess over this book – like, the ultimate kind of mess I haven’t been since reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156-six-of-crows' rel='nofollow noopener'>Six of Crows</a> and I’m screaming internally and externally from the chilling ecstasy reading this book woke in me</span>
  <span id="freeText6703261688591718306" style="display:none"><a href="https://bookishreviewsblog.blogspot.com/2019/09/nora-sakavic-raven-king-foxhole-court.html" rel="nofollow noopener">My review </a><br /><br /><i>"They were exhausted, sore, and more than a little disappointed by their loss, but the Foxes left the stadium feeling like champions.”</i><br /><br /><br />They are every fucking inch the champions. Excuse me, where can I sign the adoption papers for the entire Palmetto State University Team? I am a complete fucking mess over this book – like, the ultimate kind of mess I haven’t been since reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156-six-of-crows" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> and I’m screaming internally and externally from the chilling ecstasy reading this book woke in me (I don’t get it how my family isn’t obsessed over the characters or at least doesn’t understand my constant screeching). And now I’m stuck between procrastinating the last book because I don’t want it to end and desperately wanting to see what happens next. <br /><br /><br />This book skyrocketed above all my expectations, taking my love for sports and love for damaged characters wronged by the world to a whole different level. I am breathless, I am at a loss for words, lost in the sea of emotion this book released in me for an infinite moment that I have been reading it. There is so much about this book that makes it amazing – writing most of all, for how can you have a good book without an amazing author who knows exactly what to give his readers. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6896843.Nora_Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">Sakavic </a>illustrated life in sport – imperfect and fucked up life with a lot to work on, but the idea of that feeling of importance and belonging is still there and I cannot thank her enough for giving such a voice to a one-of-a-kind athlete.<br /><br /><br /><i>“Look. Shit happened. Shit's going to keep happening. You don't need me to tell your life isn't fair. You're here because you know it isn't. Life doesn't care what we want out of it; it's up to us to fight for what we want with everything we've got. Seth wanted us to win. He wanted us to make it past the fourth match. I think we owe it to him to perform. Let's show the world what we've got. Let's make this our year.”</i><br /><br /><br />If there is a heaven for books, this one has a throne waiting for it there. The first one was a hell of a shocker, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013-the-raven-king" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> was ten times more so. The intensity of its plot was enough to fry every single one of my brain cells – from the intense and vivid games and mafia wars to immensely complex and intertwined character interactions – this book is everything I’ll be thinking about for the rest of my life. Foxes playing together, fighting for each other and trying to overcome their differences and help each other with the trauma is something I am not ready to let go of. They are such a messed-up bunch, but what’s there is the ferocity of their characters that is still there after everything, that drives them forward to fight for their team no matter what. I don’t want to sound dramatic, but fuck me, what did I do to deserve this book?<br /><br /><br /><i>“He was their family. They were his. They were worth every cut and bruise and scream.”</i><br /><br /><br />It is so amazing how I literally can’t find one character that I don’t adore in this book – all of the Foxes completely occupied my heart and have no intention of leaving anytime soon. <b>Neil </b>Josten is the carrier of the plot and his problems keep growing. The situation with the Moriyamas is unraveling and he is in more danger than ever – only now he decided not to be afraid. The belonging that literally saved him and his love for Exy are the things that keep him fighting for his Foxes – the only thing he has left. I love every part about this sassy boy who took it upon himself to fix his team in order to take them where they all deserve to be – on the top. <br /><br /><br /><i>“Your parents are dead, you are not fine, and nothing is going to be okay. This is not news to you. But from now until May you are still Neil Josten and I am still the man who said he would keep you alive.”</i><br /><br /><br />The entire story is told from Neil's perspective as the main character but I feel like this book was mostly oriented on a strong-willed amazing creature that is <b>Andrew </b>Minyard. Geez, if you thought the first one was dark and fucked up then you're up for a treat. I finally came to understand the damage he'd undertaken and the abuse he had endured. The darkness that comes from him can only find any consolation in the need to protect what's his like no one protected him and I really want him to be better and find some purpose in Exy. <br /><br />I also have a new discovery and it's called my love for <b>Kevin</b> Day. I usually have a distaste for cowardly characters, but his will and determination, as well as despise for himself, give him a deep dimension of someone who needs to recover and get over his long-induced trauma. He pushes himself to be better when everything has been taken from him and I nominate him for the biggest cinnamon roll of the month.<br /><br /><br />But my love doesn’t stop there – no, no – there is also<b> Nicky</b> who is such an icon, fierce <b>Dan</b> and loyal <b>Matt</b>, sweet <b>Renee</b>, determined <b>Allison</b>, and even asshole <b>Aaron</b>, but they’re all part of something amazing. <br /><br /><br /><i>“Neil thought about Renee's bruised knuckles, Dan's fierce spirit, and Allison holding her ground on the court a week after Seth's death. He thought about his mother standing unflinching in the face of his father's violent anger and her ruthlessly leaving bodies in their wake. He felt compelled to say, "Some of the strongest people I've known are women.”</i><br /><br /><a href="https://bookishreviewsblog.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog </a><br /><a href="https://www.tumblr.com/blog/bookishreviewsblog" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6703261688591718306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2808239843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2808239843" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2808239843?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2808239843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3558407227488951829"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557671656ra/27494906.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> He was their family. <br/>They were his. <br/>They were worth every cut and bruise and scream. </i><br/><br/>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br/>Sometimes family comes by blood. Sometimes it’s friends, a family we choose on our own. <br/>Neil never needed friends. He never needed a family after his mother died. <br/>But after so much pain, so much work, the Foxes feel like something for Neil. <br/>Even though he does not know what he feels for them.<br/>But you can never outrun your past forever. <br/>Sometimes it’s not far away, sometimes it’ll catch you even if you</span>
  <span id="freeText3558407227488951829" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557671656ra/27494906.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> He was their family. <br>They were his. <br>They were worth every cut and bruise and scream. </i><br><br>Story 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>Sometimes family comes by blood. Sometimes it’s friends, a family we choose on our own. <br>Neil never needed friends. He never needed a family after his mother died. <br>But after so much pain, so much work, the Foxes feel like something for Neil. <br>Even though he does not know what he feels for them.<br>But you can never outrun your past forever. <br>Sometimes it’s not far away, sometimes it’ll catch you even if you try to run. <br><br>Some people aka fans say that this series get better with every book. And it’s true. <br>It does get better. The story, the characters... <br>This book was really intriguing and really really addictive. It held my attention like no other book did in a long time. <br>Yes, I wasn’t all that interested in the game itself, but the characters are what makes this series so special. <br><br>Character 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>Sometimes if you read about Neil as a character, especially from his point of view, you feel like this young boy does not feel a thing. Nothing that is normal. <br>Maybe that sounds strange, so let me explain it. <br>When Neil feels things he can’t comprehend, he’s confused and ignores them. <br>Sometimes he can’t ignore them, so he reacts to them. Sometimes aggressively, sometimes different. <br>But he reacts. <br>Yes, he thinks the other ones are not his friends, but when it comes to protecting them, he will be there in a heartbeat. <br>And with every day in his chosen family he realizes what it really means to live, to care. <br>And that exact character development makes Neil such a special but wonderful character. <br>Andrew is an extraordinary case too. Yes, he’s aggressive and nearly all of the time on his medicine, but even though he does not care that much, he cares. <br>When he thinks his friends could be hurt, he checks on them. Yes, he makes jokes about it and tries to tell it’s something different, but like Neil, he does care a lot about his chosen family. <br>More of the other characters, like Matt, Kevin, Andrew get more attention in this book and we get bits of their past and I really really like that. <br><br>Relationships 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>Yes, I’m waiting for a little love in this series. Don’t kill me for it. And even though I feel the tension, I want more.<br>But I’m really satisfied with what I got. <br>I really like that those two formed a bond and with every day, with every catastrophe that is happening, it gets stronger. <br>I’m also in love with the team Spirit the Foxes develop. In the beginning there were little groups - the Upperclassmen and Kevin’s group. But now they mix and match and little by little they form something that you really can call a team. <br>I’m so happy about that! <br><br>Writing style 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br>Ah, like I said in the first book: In my opinion there is a little bit too much talk about the sports, but it’s okay. If you really think about it, that’s how it should be. Sports - Exy is really the center of the universe for those boys. It’s what makes them really really happy. <br>Also I really like that this book is also heavily character driven. <br><br>Can’t wait for book three!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3558407227488951829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1698086866" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1698086866" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1698086866?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18743272-the-raven-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fave-couple">fave-couple</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1698086866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16419079899712479209"><i>"He was their family. They were his. They were worth every cut and bruise and scream"</i><br/> ----------------------------------------------------------------------------<br/><br/>I am honestly incapable of proper speech. This was AMAZING. This deserves ten stars. This deserves to be heralded. These books are <i>S O G O O D </i><br/><br/>This is me right about now:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382639699ra/6085930.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>MY EMOTIONS ARE NOT IN CHECK !! I AM DEAD. !!!! RIP MY SOUL. <br/><br/> <b>Okay. I'm going to try to keep it together so here's a little summary of this series.</b> <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> The Foxhole Cou</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText16419079899712479209" style="display:none"><i>"He was their family. They were his. They were worth every cut and bruise and scream"</i><br> ----------------------------------------------------------------------------<br><br>I am honestly incapable of proper speech. This was AMAZING. This deserves ten stars. This deserves to be heralded. These books are <i>S O G O O D </i><br><br>This is me right about now:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382639699ra/6085930.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>MY EMOTIONS ARE NOT IN CHECK !! I AM DEAD. !!!! RIP MY SOUL. <br><br> <b>Okay. I'm going to try to keep it together so here's a little summary of this series.</b> <br><br><i>
  <blockquote> The Foxhole Court is about alot of things. It follows Neil Josten, the son of a famous crime boss who's running from his past and his father. While hiding in a small town known as Millport, he is asked by Kevin Day to play Exy for the Palmetto Foxes. Kevin is the assistant coach of The Foxes, a renowned Exy player and also someone from Neil's past he'd very much rather avoid. <br><br>Exy is a fictional sport, a kind of hybrid between Lacrosse and Rugby which has reached widespread popularity in America. Neil, who plays as a striker (they score the goals) agrees to join The Foxes. <br><br> The Foxes are the joke of the league - while they have some talented players, they're dysfunctional - even their 'best' players have serious issues that prevent them reaching their full potential. Their players are all recruited from broken homes and some of the issues of the players prevent them from cooperating with those around them. <br><br> Their best player, Kevin Day, transferred to the Foxes after a skiing injury - this means he's unable to play properly with the hand he learnt to play with and has to retrain himself all over again. <br>Their goalkeeper, Andrew, is only able to play under the condition he be under the effects of debilitating medication. The medication regulates his violent outbursts, but it also prevents him from connecting to and establishing proper relationships with people because the medication makes him largely apathetic. Despite being one of the best goalkeepers in the league, he cares little for the game or the outcome of any match. <br><br>This makes up the general premise of the story, but very much so the story follows the characters as they develop relationships between eachother and as the dynamics in the group shift. The team is arranged in very hierarchal structures, and each character has their own place in the team. Each character also has their own unique story, history and issues. However, there is a clear and continuing plot that is enhanced rather than sabotaged by the characters which drive the narrative. <br><br>
</blockquote>
</i><br><br>I thought this book was definitely better than the last one. It had literally no slump at all, but picked up exactly where the first finished. There was NO point in this book which was more boring than anything else. Like I'd get to a section and be like "oh sigh this is going to be boring " and then NOO bOOOOOM it was one of the best bits in the book I CANNOT BELIEVE how fast paced it was. Even though it's a book which is character driven, at NO POINT is it slow. <br><br>Many of the issues I had with the first book, such as it being confusing with all the new characters/terms were resolved here simply by merit that it was the second book and I knew what was going on.<br><br>I feel like I need to address the characters since they are literally THE highlight of this whole thing. There was SO MUCH character development. I mean, I thought these characters were pretty well developed in book 1 and then Sakavic just goes and doubles, triples, QUADRUPLES the amount of character development we had. <br><br>I was so, so happy to finally hear Renee's story. Renee is such an intriguing character to me and I really love her alot. I love that she took a bigger role in this one and I liked that Neil and her finally had a proper conversation. She's such an angel. <br><br> <i>
  <blockquote> "I'm a bad person, trying very hard to be a good person. But I would not be trying at all if it were not for the outside interventions in my life.</blockquote>
</i> <br><br>I love Renee because she doesn't try to pretend to be anything she's not. I love that she recognises her past and tries to move forward from there. Nicky calls her an angel and I agree. I appreciate that her character is not undermined or "weakened" because she is nice. I love Renee alot, and I feel she's a character we don't see much, especially in ya and especially in sport centric books. <br><br>Dan and Matt were so much better in this one. Dan especially had me cackling and she's so fierce and strong. I love her &amp; admire her alot. It was nice to see her take a more prominent role in Neil's life and to see her history and backstory. I also loved that Matt was more involved with the team as a whole and that his past was also explored. I LOVED THAT HE INVITED THE MONSTERS TO CHRISTMAS. <br><br>AARON. A A R O N. SOO much development. So so much backstory and history and explanation to his shitty behaviour. He just made such an impact in this book &amp; WHEN NEIL HIGHTAILED IT THE FCUK UP TO HIM TO SORT HIM OUT fucking #bless I was so glad. But on a serious note Aaron was sort of a mysterious and weird character who groused from the sidelines and I'm glad that much more development was invested into him. His dynamic with Andrew is so incredibly heartbreaking and he's just so important to the boy and vice versa and I really need him and Andrew to sort things out. <br><br>Nicky was Nicky. He and Kevin took more of a backseat in this one but I thought it was ok. I feel they were both so involved in the first book it was nice to set them aside and hear from others. However, where they did come into play I really really enjoyed their chapters. Anything involving Erik was good when it cam to Nicky, and everything involving Andrew/the arrangement/Ravens when it came to Kevin was good too. LOVED that Nicky bridged the gap between the monsters &amp; the upperclassmen. Nicky is so important the fact he uprooted his entire life to care for Aaron/Andrew even though they're both asshole I was just .. Nicky is good people NICKY IS SO GOOD. <br><br>I wish Allison had been in it more. Thats my one character complaint. But I did really love the way she stood up at the games after what happened to Seth and I'm so proud of her she's a queen. <br><br>Ok welps getting down to the business end of the game I guess bc Andrew and Neil. <br><br>I'll start with Neil. OKay. Neil. NEIL HAS CHANGED AND GROWN AND DEVELOPED SO SO MUCH IT'S ACTUALLY BREATHTAKING. Neil has just ... it's just spectacular the amount he's grown and developed. I love that he's trusting people, I love that he's taking a prominent role in people's lives. I love that he cares &amp; loves for them. I can't believe how in 181 pages he's given SO MUCH development in a way that wasn't rushed or forced but just worked and flowed sensibly. Neil learning to trust those around him, learning to fall back on them in times of need and learning to even love them is so, so heartwarming. I feel like I've invested so much into his character already and seeing him develop positively is the best pay off it's like he's my actual son. I love that Sakavic can so easily surmount so much development into just little things. Wymack asking him "Are you okay?" And then Neil answering "No. No I'm not Coach" had be REALLY EMOTIONAL because it just showed how he's developed and how he's learning to let people in and admit he's not fine and he's willing to accept help from others it makes me sob like a proud momma. <br><br>Ok Andrew. Now we need to talk about Andrew. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468693904ra/19737796.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In many ways, this series could be described as a study of "what the fuck is it that makes Andrew Minyard tick". And man. MAN. This book gave it to me. It gave SHOVELS of it to me. (in the most upsetting, heartbreaking, distressing way) Andrew is a constant enigma, but I feel like I finally get it, I finally get him. (At least a little more than before.) And it's so, so saddening to see his story unfold because he is a good person, he really is. It's just that his goodness has been buried under alot of bullshit that happened to him. But urgh. I just feel like Andrew is such a fractured &amp; broken figure, and he really, really makes me love him and hate him and feel for him AND I WILL CRY FOR HIM IF HE DOESN'T CATCH A BREAK SOON. <br><br>------<br><br>This books just have such a way of grabbing you and drawing your attention and making you <i>care</i> Like I care so much and these are very short books. All of the foxes have captivated me. Their characterisation, the world building, the dialogue, the pacing, literally everything is perfect. This series is a blessing, and everyone should read it. <br><br>I can't wait to start book #3. I've heard it's not smooth sailing but I'm hoping they can pull through. They HAVE to beat the Edgar Allen Raven because those asshole need to GO DOWN. <br><br><b>A few gifs on my emotions in the book: </b> <br><br>When Neil hightailed it the fuck up the Aarons to sort out the mess w/ Andrew. When Neil promised to protect Kevin &amp; Andrew gave Neil his car keys and they did that gay asf shirt touching thing and Wymack was like lmfao you's are so gay and Neil was like ??? bc he's a dumb dumb (they're my otp omg) <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383850421ra/6685420.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Neil told Coach Wymack he wasn't ok and he did need help<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468693904ra/19737797.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>WHEN NEIL SHITTALKED RIKO AND THEN PUNCHED HIM <b>DIRECTLY IN THE FACE.</b> . (Also when the Foxes were allowed to play on after losing Andrew) <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468693904ra/19737798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Renee telling her story and also informing him Andrew's gay asf. Nicky getting the monsters to come to Matt's for Christmas. Andrew agreeing to Halloween with the upperclassmen. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468693904ra/19737799.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>ME WHEN I FINSIHED THE BOOK:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468693904ra/19737800.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>In conclusion I'm blown away by how good this was LOVED IT SO MUCH<br><br><a href="https://open.spotify.com/user/jamieson_k/playlist/5Bxvr7ugZ8CXLq6w3KrIh7" rel="nofollow noopener">my official foxhole court playlist bc I'm lame</a></span>

  <span id="freeText5020621332060870921" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 Stars</b><br /><br />Woah!<br /><br />'The Raven King' was even better than the 'The Foxhole Court'. <br /><br />I was not prepared for this book it was intense, heartbreaking, shocking and thrilling. <br /><br />My love these characters have grown and we learn more about them and their past. <br /><br />There were tiny hints of romance between the main character and another but I'm glad it's slow as it will create more depth and growth between them.<br /><br />Oh!   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1828294307" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1828294307?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✧ k a t i e ✧" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✧ k a t i e ✧" href="/user/show/48788301-k-a-t-i-e">✧ k a t i e ✧</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18743272-the-raven-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48788301-k-a-t-i-e?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1828294307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2603253408019746438"><i> "Death was unpleasant, but it was a familiar and tolerable ache in his chest.” </i> <br/><br/>I was a sobbing mess for majority of this book. This book made me cry, smile, and cry some more. The books that can make you feel so many emotions in less than 300 pages are the best kinds of books.<br/><br/>Where should I start? The character development? Getting to know more of Renee's, Dan's, Matt's, and Aaron's backstory? This book had everything that I wanted from the last book. There was more of the characters that I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText2603253408019746438" style="display:none"><i> "Death was unpleasant, but it was a familiar and tolerable ache in his chest.” </i> <br /><br />I was a sobbing mess for majority of this book. This book made me cry, smile, and cry some more. The books that can make you feel so many emotions in less than 300 pages are the best kinds of books.<br /><br />Where should I start? The character development? Getting to know more of Renee's, Dan's, Matt's, and Aaron's backstory? This book had everything that I wanted from the last book. There was more of the characters that I wanted to see. There is also character development for many of the characters, which I was glad to see. Can we also talk about Neil's little obsession with his new practice racquet?<br /><br /><i> "Do you have any idea how much it cost?" Neil asked. "Yes, I want it back." </i><br /><br />I love the humor in this series. I love the characters in this series. And most of all, I love how Nora Sakavic gets you so emotionally invested in both the plot and the characters.<br /><br />This series is going to kill me. <br /><br /><i> "But Neil Josten was a Fox. Andrew called this home; Nicky called him family. Neil wasn't going to lose any of it." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2603253408019746438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1629805713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1629805713" />
    <a title="Paula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16274207-paula"><img alt="Paula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603829135p2/16274207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1629805713?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula" href="/user/show/16274207-paula">Paula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anybody that wants to feel like they're taking crazy pills</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1629805713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2609157754722335712">This book is terrible. Not even like the first one, that one was terrible in a fun way. This one is so bad it's offensive. <br/><br/>To be perfectly honest, it wouldn't bother me this much if it didn't have a FOUR POINT FORTY SIX STARS OUT OF FIVE rating on this website. That is insane. I feel like I got some bootleg .mobi of this thing and I've been reading a whole entire different book. My version of The Raven King reads like dark!Harry Drarry AU taken from a livejournal community in 2005, not a 4.46/5 </span>
  <span id="freeText2609157754722335712" style="display:none">This book is terrible. Not even like the first one, that one was terrible in a fun way. This one is so bad it's offensive. <br /><br />To be perfectly honest, it wouldn't bother me this much if it didn't have a FOUR POINT FORTY SIX STARS OUT OF FIVE rating on this website. That is insane. I feel like I got some bootleg .mobi of this thing and I've been reading a whole entire different book. My version of The Raven King reads like dark!Harry Drarry AU taken from a livejournal community in 2005, not a 4.46/5 book. I am honestly shaken up about it. Am I stupid? Did I miss something? Has everyone gone mad?<br /><br />Let's dissect this thing, I guess. <br /><br />First of all, the writing itself. Goddamnit, I swear I don't need to know where every character is sitting every time Neil enters a room. That's not how you paint a picture, by describing sitting arrangements. I don't need to know how they sat in the bus, if Allison was in the first row with Renee and Matt and Dan where in the row behind them and Abby was wherever the hell she was. It doesn't even matter! Neil sat between Kevin and Andrew, didn't he? Just say that, don't waste 500 words on soulless description. Also, a full paragraph of five word sentences is the fastest way to make me doze off and have my kindle fall on my face. That was fun.<br /><br />Then, the characters. Neil keeps being insufferable. He's the most unsympathetic main character I've come across in a minute. Am I supposed to care about what happens to him? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He has this ability to make everything about him. When that dude rapes Andrew (and that's a whole 'nother mess, we'll get into it later) somehow everyone is worrying about him. Andrew got raped, Aaron killed a guy, Nicky got screwed by his parents once again, and we're supposed to feel for Neil? Get outta here, man.<br /><br />And he somehow is this savior figure, The Uniter Of Teams, The Protector Of Kevins, The Thawer Of Frozen Andrew Hearts or some shit. It's a mystery to me how anyone even stands him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Andrew and his mental illness. Oh, boy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mood stabilizers still don't work like that. If you take pills to help with your psychosis, or whatever it is Andrew has, I don't know exactly what they do, but I'm pretty damn sure they don't make you so manic you have a laughing fit while getting raped. What the actual fuck. Like ??¡? what. <br /><br />I read somewhere that this lady spent 13 years writing and revising this series before publishing. Didn't she have a couple of hours to spare to Google about mental illness? She just made up a random condition that makes no sense just for the sake of making him dark and dangerous. We all love a bad boy, don't we? One clinically insane that keeps almost stabbing everyone with his hidden ninja knives. Gotta get me a man like that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Kevin keeps being the most interesting. His struggle and his motivations are a lot more deserving of reading about that Neil's or Andrew's nonsense. Andrew and Aaron's relationship could be interesting too, if it wasn't explained to us in such a muddled way. A lot of the times we learn about characters through third-party explanations. It's so lazy and so confusing, especially when Neil starts to make connections in his mind he doesn't talk the reader through. A lot of the times I asked myself what even was happening, if I had already met this characters they were talking about, because I honestly couldn't be bothered with learning a thousand names and a thousand backstories. Half of them didn't serve any purpose, too.<br /><br />Now, my favorite part of the whole thing, The Almighty Ravens! The cartooniest villains. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They live in a basement. The stadium is black, the rooms are black, the sheets and the towels are black because they're so Dark and Bad and Villain-y. They all dress the same way, too. because the whole thing wasn't idiotic enough. Jesus. And their super intense interactions with Neil and the Foxes, so Dark! so Intense! That dialogue, that murderous back and forth! Hilarious. So cliché.<br /><br />Also, I just love how the coach is evil just for the sake of being evil. His brother is Yakuza, so he just invented a weird sport and he now bullies teenagers mercilessly. Makes total sense. He's a fleshed out character for sure. Riko too. This book is full to the brim with rich characters that have complex motivations.<br /><br />That was sarcasm. They're all one dimensional and everything is absurd. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Now, the plot. Wowie.<br /><br />I think the author has this problem where she thinks "you know what would be cool? X and Y and Z." And she finds a way to get the characters to X and Y and Z without worrying about having it make sense in the context of the story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like with Neil going to the Raven's college for two weeks. She wanted Neil to go there and be tortured for some reason, so she did it. She sold it as a way for him to protect Andrew from that crooked psychiatrist we didn't know about two seconds ago. Because it makes so much sense that a college Exy coach orchestrated the rape of a dude by his former foster brother, and he somehow knew he would be committed into a mental institution so he bought off a doctor that was willing to kill a patient, just so he could have Neil train with them for two weeks and then let him go home just like that. That is the most absurd thing I have ever read, I am honestly speechless. And Neil is like "yeah, that makes sense, let me go spend the Christmas break with you, I'll catch the first plane tomorrow." That makes absolutely zero sense, not just to any sane reader, but also in the context of Neil's character development (or lack thereof).<br /><br />Andrew's rape is even worse in that regard. They come to this house to have an awkward family meal and the mom is like "yeah, Andrew, I have a surprise bottle of booze in a room upstairs, why don't you go and get it." Because that's a thing that happens, apparently. So he goes, and his former foster brother and sexual abuser is there, so he gets raped. Just like that. In a nice suburban house with some family having a roast dinner downstairs. Blood everywhere, too, not even a discreet raping, he really goes for it.<br /><br />As shock value goes, that's a really fucking cheap move. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway, to summarize, everything is terrible and this book is the worst. See you in my review of the third one, I'm having so much fun getting mad at his series and this goddamned website. Y'all crazy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2609157754722335712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1656107447" />
    <a title="Simone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16882244-simone"><img alt="Simone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531247180p2/16882244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1656107447?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simone" href="/user/show/16882244-simone">Simone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18743272-the-raven-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=athletes-sports">athletes-sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1656107447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15615507749941077201"><b>'Reread' via audiobook December 2018: Gahhhh, listening to it made the whole thing even more intense... </b>❤️<br/>-----------------------------------------<br/><br/><b>Out for revenge!</b><br/><br/>Just to make it clear: by that I mean myself! <br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472458871ra/20195264.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>Normally, I’m a peace-loving human being and I’ve read a lot of books that made me angry, but last night I was ready to commit a murder! Of a book character! My very first update of the first book in this series said that I already hate the guts of Riko, although I haven’t even met him.</span>
  <span id="freeText15615507749941077201" style="display:none"><b>'Reread' via audiobook December 2018: Gahhhh, listening to it made the whole thing even more intense... </b>❤️<br>-----------------------------------------<br><br><b>Out for revenge!</b><br><br>Just to make it clear: by that I mean myself! <br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472458871ra/20195264.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Normally, I’m a peace-loving human being and I’ve read a lot of books that made me angry, but last night I was ready to commit a murder! Of a book character! My very first update of the first book in this series said that I already hate the guts of Riko, although I haven’t even met him. And my gut feeling did not deceive me, not in the slightest. Riko is said Raven King, leader of the opposing team of the Foxes, part of the Japanese mafia and connected to Neil’s past. I would have thought to sleep on the matter would calm me down, but just the thought of the things Riko did to Neil at the end of this book gets my blood pressure skyrocketing to a dangerous level…<br><br>But books that bring out such strong emotions are simply the best and I experienced the whole range of feelings while reading this one. I laughed about the dry comments of the coach (I simply love this grumpy bastard! ;-), I rooted for the team during their games, I was shocked about things that came to light and some situations almost made me cry. <br><br>I was so glad when the team finally did act like a <i>team</i>, on and off the court. <br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472458871ra/20195265.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>It was about time, although something bad had to happen first to open their eyes. But I guess with a team made of fucked-up kids whose individual pasts consists of secrets, lies and abuse, trust is something they have got to learn and it is not easily earned, either. Speaking of the past… Parts of Neil’s and Andrew’s past are finally revealed in this book due to half-truths, unwelcome disclosures and those shocking situations I mentioned earlier. The outcome will keep me on the edge of my seat during the next book, I suppose.<br><br>In case you expect this…<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484412324i/21716502.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Well, I’m sorry to disappoint you, but you won’t see it in this book, either. But I can assure you, it would not feel right now. There are things that have to be solved first and I can’t wait to see Andrew when he is off his medication. Only then it would feel <i>real</i>. <br><br>One thing is for sure: if I won’t get my revenge in form of Neil and his Foxes taking apart the sick and sadistic asshole named Riko and his Ravens in the next book, you will hear me scream and throwing my Kindle across the room, wherever you are! ;-)<br><br><i>This review has been posted on <a href="https://dirtybooksobsessiongroup.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Dirty Books Obsession</a> </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15615507749941077201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2431673693?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18743272-the-raven-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=college">college</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=sports-romance">sports-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=trilogy">trilogy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2431673693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7968282336064678351">SECOND READ AUGUST 2019<br/><br/>_______________________________<br/><br/><br/><br/>I’m still as obsessed with this series, as I was when reading book one – Foxhole Court.<br/><br/>The plot’s complexity has quadrupled. Every character has an agenda, and many characters have pasts that are buried so deeply under lies that each discovery only cements my belief that this series is phenomenally awesome.<br/><br/>The author is a master storyteller, her way of spinning a fascinating as well as emotional tale is outstanding. Nothing in these books is </span>
  <span id="freeText7968282336064678351" style="display:none">SECOND READ AUGUST 2019<br><br>_______________________________<br><br><br><br>I’m still as obsessed with this series, as I was when reading book one – Foxhole Court.<br><br>The plot’s complexity has quadrupled. Every character has an agenda, and many characters have pasts that are buried so deeply under lies that each discovery only cements my belief that this series is phenomenally awesome.<br><br>The author is a master storyteller, her way of spinning a fascinating as well as emotional tale is outstanding. Nothing in these books is predictable. Each new discovery is more outrages and in your face than the other. Throughout the first two books my jaw hit the floor countless times. The intricacies between the different plots are mind boggling. There are just some authors that are leap years ahead of others. And Nora Sakavic is one of them. This author and series deserves way more recognition than other hyped authors and series.<br><br>When you get down to it, the entire series is one long book. Raven King started exactly where Foxhole Court ended. The team finally understands that only united they have a chance to win the final match. And seeing them growing closer, socializing and spending their free time together outside of the court is heart-warming. Because I love them all, I want them to get along.<br><br>Neil, my favorite character’s journey has been heart wrenching, but I’m also so proud of him. He’s come such a long way, and his progress makes me cheer for him even more. His relationship with Andrew is as fascinating as it is mysterious. He has this unbelievable way with him, that none of the team can get even close to. Even though they constantly battle over truths, lies, and secrets, at the end they are just trying to understand the other person. It’s quite fascinating for me as well as for them, because they each are fascinated by one another.<br><br>Raven King ended with two major arcs, and I can’t wait to read how these two arcs play into Neil and Andrew’s relationship.<br><br>I’m not going to write much more, I just want to get back to reading The King’s Men. So all I can say is read this series, actually buy it. The first book is free on Amazon, the second and third only cost 99 cents each. That’s an incredible deal. Honestly it’s ridiculous. So one-click NOW!!!<br><br><br>✵ ✦ ✷ ✫ ✷ ✦ ✧ ✵ ✧ ✵ ✦ ✷ ✫ ✷ ✦ ✧ ✵ ✧ ✵ ✦ ✷ ✫ ✷ ✦ ✧ ✵ ✧ ✵ <br><br>If you want to chat with me about books, find me on <a href="https://www.instagram.com/booktwinsreviews1/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499463307i/23236552._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more of my reviews:<br><a href="http://www.booktwinsreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog: Book Twins Reviews</a><br> <a href="https://www.facebook.com/TJLovesBooksBlog/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br> <a href="https://twitter.com/2booktwins" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a><br> <a href="http://www.booktwinsreviews.com/?page_id=142" rel="nofollow noopener">Subscribe to Blog</a></span>
