<div id="review_1784640617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1784640617" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56662187-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539790744p2/56662187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1784640617?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/56662187-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784640617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5954017682563880495">Wow okay. The ending of this book...I just...okay.<br/><br/>The All For the Game series has triggers for almost everything: abuse, rape, self-harm, addiction, violence. And yet, I finished this book smiling like an idiot. It's heavy, for sure, because it tackles series trauma, and these kids' lives have been hell, BUT the overall feeling I get while reading them is happiness. I feel uplifted. Now, my tolerance for violence and such is admittedly high. What I'm trying to communicate is that the author does</span>
  <span id="freeText5954017682563880495" style="display:none">Wow okay. The ending of this book...I just...okay.<br /><br />The All For the Game series has triggers for almost everything: abuse, rape, self-harm, addiction, violence. And yet, I finished this book smiling like an idiot. It's heavy, for sure, because it tackles series trauma, and these kids' lives have been hell, BUT the overall feeling I get while reading them is happiness. I feel uplifted. Now, my tolerance for violence and such is admittedly high. What I'm trying to communicate is that the author doesn't throw in these heavy things just to move the story along or just to add tension. I get the feeling that she does it thoughtfully. <br /><br />In this second book, we get to see Neil in a new way. He's starting to break down his walls, and let his team mates in. What he did for Andrew at the end broke my heart. I balled my eyes out when he admitted that he was not okay, when he asked Wymack to help him. <br /><br />In the first book, I loved Neil. I loved Andrew, but I wasn't all that invested in the other characters. At least not on the same level. After The Raven King, HAH! I am completely obsessed with every character. Nicky is definitely a favorite. He has such a big heart and somehow manages to love Andrew, Aaron, Kevin and all the monsters. His desire to be friends with everyone is adorable. When Neil asked him if they were friends, I cried a bit tbh. <br />Kevin with his obsession for Exy and his reluctance to stand up to Riko despite everything. Aaron and his complicated feelings for his twin Andrew. Matt and his protectiveness for Neil, Kevin, Dan, and pretty much human except Andrew. DAN. That girl is a queen and I respect her so much. <br /><br />Overall, I loved the development we saw in this book. I loved seeing the team come together more, and see Neil become a more permanent part of it. This is the kind of book that you cannot put down, and when you do put it down you spend all your time thinking about it. I can't wait to read the last book and see how everything is wrapped up because at this point I'm not sure where our characters are going. Wherever it is they go, I'm there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5954017682563880495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2490670456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2490670456" />
    <a title="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench"><img alt="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580443293p2/12766897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2490670456?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" href="/user/show/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench">Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=boys-who-like-boys">boys-who-like-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=boo-yah-straight-butter-baby">boo-yah-straight-butter-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=source-amazon-audible">source-amazon-audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2490670456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7701963644846920533"><b>Re-listen 2/2019</b><br/><br/>ugh, Riko can...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549494553ra/27026030.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Can't wait for his bitch ass to get his. Oops. Spoiler alert?<br/><br/>Really <i>still</i> not digging Cendese's voice for Andrew which also seems to be the same as Nicki's and sometimes Aaron's and even to a certain extent Riko's???? <br/><br/><b>WHY GOD, WHY?????????????</b><br/><br/>He's also not differentiating ANY of the female's voices so... that's fun to keep up with. <---sarcasm.<br/><br/>But guess what? I already started <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23594461.The_King_s_Men__All_for_the_Game___3_' title='The King's Men (All for the Game, #3) by Nora Sakavic' rel='nofollow noopener'>The King's Men</a>. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549494553ra/27026031.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Don't send them yet! Just one more boooooooooooooooooooooooooooooooookkk</span>
  <span id="freeText7701963644846920533" style="display:none"><b>Re-listen 2/2019</b><br><br>ugh, Riko can...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549494553ra/27026030.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Can't wait for his bitch ass to get his. Oops. Spoiler alert?<br><br>Really <i>still</i> not digging Cendese's voice for Andrew which also seems to be the same as Nicki's and sometimes Aaron's and even to a certain extent Riko's???? <br><br><b>WHY GOD, WHY?????????????</b><br><br>He's also not differentiating ANY of the female's voices so... that's fun to keep up with. &lt;---sarcasm.<br><br>But guess what? I already started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23594461.The_King_s_Men__All_for_the_Game___3_" title="The King's Men (All for the Game, #3) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The King's Men</a>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549494553ra/27026031.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Don't send them yet! Just one more boooooooooooooooooooooooooooooooookkkkkkkkkkkkkkkkkkk.........<br><br>*echoes as Cupcake runs away from interventionists*<br><br><b>🐾🐾🐾🐾🐾🐾REVIEW OF THE ENTIRE SERIES🐾🐾🐾🐾🐾🐾</b> <br><br>Undoubtedly superlatives will fail me in this review. Thankfully, there are eleventy-seven lazillion other reviews so I will <i>try</i> to keep this short. Try, being the operative word.<br><br>I would say I loved this series but considering it has consumed my life for the past several days, robbed me of sleep and occupied my thoughts, "loved" feels insufficient. <b>It became my obsession.</b> <br><br>For anyone who hasn't read it, I do believe this originally was one big fic that due to its whopping size (clocks in at just over 1200 pgs) was broken up into 3 books for publication. I say this because <b>I believe it was meant to be read as one story. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court__All_for_the_Game___1_" title="The Foxhole Court (All for the Game, #1) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foxhole Court</a> isn't meant to be read as a standalone</b>. It will likely leave you wanting due to some horrific shenanigans that occur amongst the Foxes. I'm not ever going to condone the events but somewhere during <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013.The_Raven_King__All_for_the_Game___2_" title="The Raven King (All for the Game, #2) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> I <b>understood</b> why they did what they did. Nevertheless, it is 1/3 of the story and only reading it is a disservice to the story arc as a whole.<br><br>Primarily because Neil's first love is Exy and through Exy he's introduced to the other great love of his life, so if you're a romance reader like me you gotta stick it out. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court__All_for_the_Game___1_" title="The Foxhole Court (All for the Game, #1) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foxhole Court</a> illustrates his undying passion for the game to perfection. He fell in love with Exy as a boy. Circumstances of his life stripped it from him and then through a series of events gave it back. In a vain effort to give his life some meaning after he's lost everything he lets himself have Exy again as a high school senior at a small school in Millport, Arizona.<br><br>He never in a million years thought his play at a an unfamiliar position as a walk on would put him on Palmetto State University's radar. But it did.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534721636i/26158787._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>David Wymack, coach of the Foxes, and his team have some rather unorthodox recruitment tactics but they succeed in signing their new striker and getting him to South Carolina in the end. <br><br><b>While Neil reacquaints himself with his love of Exy, I fell in love with Neil.</b> Trust me, no one was more surprised by this development with a character like Andrew hanging around but it's true. Neil has lived through hell, literally, and somehow someway he's retained a fundamental kindness and selflessness. He's the most resilient character I can remember ever reading about. He's not going to quit. Not ever. Exy's the only thing that's ever given him anything back and he's going to give it his all until he's got nothing left. A gamer through and through and that sort of passion has a way of galvanizing a team. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534721636i/26158788._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He brought tears to my eyes with his devotion and loyalty to the Foxes. He will sacrifice himself time and time again for them. Course his mouth puts them in the crosshairs more than once but I loved that he wasn't going to let his fear stop him from protecting them or stand in the way of his dream. <br><br>His passion and drive make them more of a cohesive unit than they've ever been which makes their small, rag tag team that's been ignored and discounted by <b>everyone</b> more dangerous than anyone could've foreseen. It also nets Neil something he's never had before: a family. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534721636i/26158789._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That hit two of my most treasured reading experiences: making a family and team unity. <br><br><b><i>All for the Game</i> is heavily weighted in sport.</b> If you are a sports fan and this book doesn't get your adrenaline pumping... I... *shrugs* I don't even know what to say. As a huge sports fan, I'm not embarrassed to say that a couple games made me verklempt. It's the classic tale of David vs. Goliath. They're outnumbered. They're inexperienced. But they've got heart, grit and determination. <b>And they've got each other.</b><br><br>Exy has brought these people together but they also share a checkered and varying degrees of horrific pasts which makes them connecting with one other (at times) challenging. Neil is very intelligent but he's also oblivious when it comes to recognizing other's actions for what they are. So it's left to the reader to decipher and decode those actions through Neil's self-abasing prism. <br><br>There isn't a lot of <b>
  <i>overt</i>
</b> romance. Neil sees his future as a finite entity and everything in his life up to now has been evanescent, as is life on the run. But as he finds his place amongst the Foxes you can see hope flicker to life. He begins to trust them and finds himself increasingly drawn to another.<br><br>These two are unquestionably soulmates but they have absolutely no idea how traditional romantic relationships work nor, I suspect, would they be interested in engaging in that sort of squishy marshmallowness. Truthfully, they would be nowhere near as interesting if they were. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>He didn't know what this thing between them was anymore. He didn't know what he wanted or needed it to be. He just knew he had to hold on for as long as he could.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>There is very little sex content (lots of kissing and one oral scene that's not titillating) but there is a <u>WHOLE LOT OF VIOLENCE</u>. Be forewarned. The bad wrong starts in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court__All_for_the_Game___1_" title="The Foxhole Court (All for the Game, #1) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foxhole Court</a>, gets worse in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013.The_Raven_King__All_for_the_Game___2_" title="The Raven King (All for the Game, #2) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> and made me MURDEROUS! With the dramatic conclusion occurring in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23594461.The_King_s_Men__All_for_the_Game___3_" title="The King's Men (All for the Game, #3) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The King's Men</a> which made my skin crawl. I'll just say, it wasn't anywhere near bloody enough for my tastes. But I am a vengeful bitch. <br><br>Fear not, it does end happily for more than just the primary couple. I don't think it's possible to read this and not become invested in all of these characters. They are all layered and complex and have surprises up their sleeves.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534721636i/26158790._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Is this series perfect? Nope. It could've been paired down, it's sometimes redundant, the game of Exy is a fictional one but the rules of the game weren't given until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013.The_Raven_King__All_for_the_Game___2_" title="The Raven King (All for the Game, #2) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a>. I don't know how the NCAA wouldn't have cracked down on the Ravens antics long ago nor can I fathom how these players could perform optimally after the way they treat their bodies <b>(trigger warning for drug usage)</b>. Some of the events are far-fetched, outlandish even and one thing in Neil's backstory just doesn't not add up for me.<br><br>But I'll tell you what, it's says something to me if a story can sink its teeth into me like this one has and <i>that</i> is something I can't discount. Not only could I not put it down, but... I can't even believe I'm about to say this after 1200+ pgs, but I'm sad it's over and I wish there were more. #certifiable <br><br>So I'll be burning an audible credit soon (possibly three depending on how the first one goes) so I can re-experience this once more when it releases. Here's hoping the narrator doesn't fuck it up.<br><br>Believe the hype. 13K+ ratings/reviews and an average of over 4 stars isn't a lie.<br><br>Original "review":<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[If someone doesn't put this son of a bitch &amp; all his kin in the cage they belong in could they send them my way?<br><br>Please. Send them my way.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534560341ra/26148137.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still withholding rating/review essentially because I think this was one big fic that got busted up into 3 books to publish due to it's length, so I'm just going to review the whole shebang once I've finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23594461.The_King_s_Men__All_for_the_Game___3_" title="The King's Men (All for the Game, #3) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The King's Men</a>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15559809532285558709">06 August 2020<br/><br/>RTC<br/><br/><br/>Two words: Andrew. Minyard. 😭 <br/><br/>No, seriously. This book contains one of the most disturbing things I have ever read.<br/><br/>This is what I wrote when I read THAT scene:<br/><blockquote>I was so terrified for him I read those pages with my hands in front of my mouth, almost crying and screaming and now, an hour later my body is still trembling and my pulse just can't calm down.<br/>I'm at school, but can't function at all, and I know I won't be able to today. My head is empty, I can't think of anything except </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15559809532285558709" style="display:none">06 August 2020<br /><br />RTC<br /><br /><br />Two words: Andrew. Minyard. 😭 <br /><br />No, seriously. This book contains one of the most disturbing things I have ever read.<br /><br />This is what I wrote when I read THAT scene:<br /><blockquote>I was so terrified for him I read those pages with my hands in front of my mouth, almost crying and screaming and now, an hour later my body is still trembling and my pulse just can't calm down.<br />I'm at school, but can't function at all, and I know I won't be able to today. My head is empty, I can't think of anything except them. <br />These characters are everything, and I want to be there to protect them.</blockquote><br />I'll never forget that feeling. I have never felt dread before while reading a book, and I'm not sure I needed to experience it, but it made this series my all time favourite, so I won't complain. But I was actually scared to death when I realized what's happening. And even now, months later, it's enough to think of it, I'm already fighting with my tears.</span>

<div id="review_1784160006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1784160006" />
    <a title="prag ♻" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29249069-prag"><img alt="prag ♻" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598781220p2/29249069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1784160006?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prag ♻" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prag ♻" href="/user/show/29249069-prag">prag ♻</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15421865235474842513"><i> “i am a bad person trying very hard to be a good person.” </i><br/><br/>ehhh, sometimes i wonder what’s either wrong with me or if i’m actually reading the same book as other people are, and this was one of those cases. this book was even worse than the previous one concerning the disjointed writing style, while i had super high hopes for that aspect since i’ve heard plenty of people i trust say that that really improves visibly. i couldn’t quite see that, honestly. which i also absolutely hated was that eve</span>
  <span id="freeText15421865235474842513" style="display:none"><i> “i am a bad person trying very hard to be a good person.” </i><br /><br />ehhh, sometimes i wonder what’s either wrong with me or if i’m actually reading the same book as other people are, and this was one of those cases. this book was even worse than the previous one concerning the disjointed writing style, while i had super high hopes for that aspect since i’ve heard plenty of people i trust say that that really improves visibly. i couldn’t quite see that, honestly. which i also absolutely hated was that every single sentence starts with a character’s name. it’s literally all just like <i>andrew did this, neil thought this, matt said this</i>. hate that.<br /><br />the first plot point started one third through the book and lasted for one single chapter. following that, there was no plot for a whole another third and i was just really bored. the pace picked up in the last four chapters or so, which left me intrigued enough for the final installment, but that’s pretty much it. also funny how i, as a non-native english speaker, found several typos and grammatical errors that also really bugged the hell out of me. all in all, i’m just very glad for this to be over cause i never felt the urge whatsoever to pick it up to continue reading. let’s see how i’ll feel about the final book, whenever i get to that one.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>→ 3 stars</i>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896994447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14123720915730571931"><i> Continuation buddy read with my lovelies ♡♡ <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/54010598-kazzexual' rel='nofollow noopener'>Em</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13306676-silvia' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sil</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Praggs</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10502567-jiana' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jia</a> ♡♡ </i><br/><br/><br/>I don’t know how this happened, but I’m kind of <s>mildly</s> obsessed with this series. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485958673i/21864948.png' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Everything that the previous book lacked, this book made up for a million times over. We had action and tears and pain, oh so much pain. I’m still wiping my tears as I write this review. <br/><br/><i> “He was content to watch and imagine. Lonely, too, but there was nothing he could do about that.” </i><br/><br/>As I mentioned in my previous review, these Foxhole kids ar</span>
  <span id="freeText14123720915730571931" style="display:none"><i> Continuation buddy read with my lovelies ♡♡ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/54010598-kazzexual" rel="nofollow noopener">Em</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13306676-silvia" rel="nofollow noopener">Sil</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya" rel="nofollow noopener">Praggs</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10502567-jiana" rel="nofollow noopener">Jia</a> ♡♡ </i><br><br><br>I don’t know how this happened, but I’m kind of <s>mildly</s> obsessed with this series. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485958673i/21864948.png" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everything that the previous book lacked, this book made up for a million times over. We had action and tears and pain, oh so much pain. I’m still wiping my tears as I write this review. <br><br><i> “He was content to watch and imagine. Lonely, too, but there was nothing he could do about that.” </i><br><br>As I mentioned in my previous review, these Foxhole kids are the opposite of nice (well except for Matty, what a darling) but in this book we got an extra insight as to <i> what </i> made them so cruel and dark. And damn did it destroy me. <br><br>There is so much character development happening along with the plot. These kids who come from messed up homes are slowly learning what it means to trust and belong and have a family that you choose rather than are born into. <br><br>This is some deep ish here, someone hold me. <br><br>Look at my babies:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485958673i/21864949.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Can we just give a special medal to Coach Wymack for his outstand mothering skills with this mess of a team? So much #goals. <br><br><br>I’m so heartbroken and shattered by this book. I need a minute – or a lot of minutes. <br><br>I just – I just feel so much emotions for these children and I cannot help but cry and cheer for them at every moment. They’ve come so far from what they used to be omg I’m so proud of my children. <br><br><br>OKAY, SO I SAW THIS ON TUMBLR AND COULDN’T HELP BUT POST (I laughed for a few years)– THIS IS WHAT SHOULD HAVE HAPPENED !!! (not really a spoiler but I’m still tagging) <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485958673i/21864950.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485958673i/21864951.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485958673i/21864952._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a href="http://berry-muffin.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">(s)</a>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br>Onto the next book, can’t wait for more pain. :) :) :)<br><br><i> “They were exhausted, sore, and more than a little disappointed by their loss, but the Foxes left the stadium feeling like champions.” </i><br><br>5 stars!!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1636708820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4934661728866128811"><b>Re-read August 2020</b><br/>I can't get enough of these.<br/><br/>---------------------------------<br/><br/>This is one of my favorite series. I cannot recommend these books enough. <br/><br/>Neil is still at Palmetto State University, playing Exy with his team of outcasts. We learn a lot more about Neil’s background and Kevin and Andrew learn some of his secrets.<br/><br/>The Raven team is still their enemy and Riko does everything to destroy Neil and Kevin. I wanted to stab Riko, over and over again. He is so evil. The things he did to Kevi</span>
  <span id="freeText4934661728866128811" style="display:none"><b>Re-read August 2020</b><br>I can't get enough of these.<br><br>---------------------------------<br><br>This is one of my favorite series. I cannot recommend these books enough. <br><br>Neil is still at Palmetto State University, playing Exy with his team of outcasts. We learn a lot more about Neil’s background and Kevin and Andrew learn some of his secrets.<br><br>The Raven team is still their enemy and Riko does everything to destroy Neil and Kevin. I wanted to stab Riko, over and over again. He is so evil. The things he did to Kevin, Andrew and Neil…..<br><br>It was just brutal.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463206663ra/19092601.gif" width='380"' height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really love how dark everything feels. But I’m also glad that Neil finally allows himself to have friends, even though he doesn’t know what to do with that. And the thing at the end…. what he did for Andrew… My heart broke..<br><br>These books are a violent, psychotic mess and I loved every second of it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463206663ra/19092602.gif" width='380"' height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4934661728866128811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PciiurPVoirk9zNl4ksLIhdGIe/stQCNdeRrHyvd8MJ5IJgUCE1HMwEej0N2MuDcQegi7njYC9Cdj0AIogbAWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F0zDIxWd3ruE226Kax8pM8aZdU++svags3zymoJfRSJTpPmNrgU7omEy0qz/ZsLNkDd2Tirf/f1bF9mNC4R1uA==')})
  }
//]]>
